From prem at songbirdtech.com  Mon Apr 16 20:36:47 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Mon Apr 16 20:37:09 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Re: GNU/Linux trouble
Message-ID: <1398.61.247.255.57.1176736007.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

>> There have been multiple upgrades to the Windows XP kernel and the
>> subsystems. Service Pack 1, and Pack 2 were major upgrades, besides these
>> there have been many, many more.

>Actually, you will find that very very few patches are directly made to
>the kernel itself - the Windows kernel runs very different from the
>Linux one.

You are right in that the Linux kernel and Windows kernel are implemented
very differently with Windows XP (not 95/98) implemented as a microkernel
with a lot of the functionality implemented using subsystems.

However, Windows service pack updates do change kernels as well. For
instance, Service Pack 2 update included support in the kernel for
additional memory protection including DEP (Date Execution Protection).
>From Microsoft's page on this:

"Data execution prevention (DEP) is a set of hardware and software
technologies that perform additional checks on memory to help protect
against malicious code exploits.  In Windows XP SP2, DEP is enforced by
both hardware and software."

Please see:
http://www.microsoft.com/technet/prodtechnol/winxppro/maintain/sp2mempr.mspx


> Also, technically SP1 and SP2 were considered to be different
>releases as far as I know. And I do recall there being a lot of noise
>about drivers not working on SP2 when it came out initially. Sort of
>like the new Vista stuff - its taken them almost a year and half to get
>*some* of the drivers working right, a lot of hardware out there is
>still not really running ok on Vista.

If your statement that windows does not make kernel-level updates is to be
believed, how is that you claim that windows service pack updates cause
problems with drivers?

>"a lot of hardware out there is still not really running ok on Vista."

Please list one or two. My point is not that these service pack updates
work perfectly. Occassionally, service pack updates will cause disruptions
with the drivers. However, that is an exception and not the rule. A
service pack update has yet to cause *ALL* the users to download *ALL* the
drivers.

With Linux, when you install Linux kernel via yum update, you will also
download the driver modules for that version. That is, you will be
downloading *ALL* the drivers for that version of Linux that comes as
standard with the Linux kernel tree.

>> The reason you didn't notice that these were kernel upgrades proves my
>> point that the MS update mechanism for kernels works well.

>You have this very wrong. MS dont update and add functionality at that
>level of the system once its released. You never see the -devel or
>-trunk version of the Windows system level at all. you only see whats
>been released and called stable from them. What you are doing here is
>comparing an evolutionary process of the Linux kernel development to the
>waterfall process of the Windows system.

This statement makes no sense. I made no comparison between the
development models of Linux and Windows and in anycase that has no bearing
on the discussion.

>>> This is absolutely not true. eg,. I've had a stable driver on my home
>>> server for the 3ware 9550sx working fine for almost 2 years now ( the
>
>> You can install compile drivers provided with *source* into the kernel if
>> you have the kernel headers without recompiling the entire kernel. But if
>> you don't have the source for the driver, you are out of luck.

>It seems from your statements that you havent really ever used a stable
>distro before ? Could I ask what distro you really use ?

I have used Linux since 1994 and I have used a variety of distros starting
with slackware, Redhat, Suse, Mandrake, Vector, Fedora Core x etc.

>I actually meant what I said, I have a single binary kernel module that
>drives my 3ware 9550, without needing a recompile, for 2 years and its
>seem quite a few kernels. I dont even need to do anything at all beyond
>a yum update kernel. The machine has no kernel-devel or kernel sources (
>also, you dont usually need the complete kernel-sources to build
>drivers, you should only need the headers - there are a few exceptions
>though )

You seem to be unaware that all Linux kernel releases from 2.4.3 already
includes the 3ware 9550 driver.

I restate myself here - when you install Linux kernel via yum update, you
will also download the driver modules for that version. That is, you will
be downloading *ALL* the drivers for that version of Linux that comes as
standard with the Linux kernel tree. Yum would have downloaded the binary
version of the driver.

If 3ware 9550 *BINARY* drivers are compatible across kernels, why are they
providing these kernel specific driver downloads?

See:
http://www.3ware.com/kb/article.aspx?id=14546

For clarity and emphasis - There is NO SUPPORT in Linux for *BINARY*
drivers which work across kernel releases. If the source driver for 3ware
9550 did not exist as part of the Linux kernel, you would have had to
download and install a binary version of the 3ware 9550 driver for each
version of linux kernel that you use.

Both ATI as well as NVIDIA provide binary drivers but they utilize a
work-around to solve this problem of lack of support for binary drivers.

Both Nvidia and ATI utilize what are known as "Kernel Interface Layers".
These "Kernel Interface Layers" are compiled during the installation of
the drivers from either ATI or Nvidia and for this the Kernel Headers must
be present on disk. These kernel interface layers provide the interface to
the binary drivers.

Besides the kernel interface layer provided as source, Nvidia (I am not
sure about ATI) now comes with precompiled  kernel interface layers for
the popular linux kernel releases. The driver installer will choose what
precompiled kernel interface layer to use during installation time. If a
precompiled interface layer is not available for the version of Linux
kernel installed on your machine (even if it is just a point difference),
the installer will attempt to recompile the kernel interface layer code
for that version of the kernel. That is the reason the kernel headers must
reside on your machine.

See:
http://us.download.nvidia.com/XFree86/Linux-x86/1.0-9755/README/chapter-02-section-03.html

For ATI:
http://ati.amd.com/support/drivers/linux/linux-radeon.html

NOTE: Please notice the text on this page that mandates that kernel
headers are required if the entire kernel source is not present.

Also see:
http://linuxhelp.150m.com/ati/ati.htm

So my point:

1. No, Linux does not support *pure* binary drivers without an
intermediate layer which must be compiled separately for each point
release of the kernel.

2. Please take time to do some research first. Any of what I have pointed
out could have been verified if you had bothered to take 15 minutes to
research it.

3. I have used Linux for 13 odd years now. But whether I have used Linux
for a day or a hundred years doesn't matter. What matters is if I what I
am saying is true or not. Judge what is said based on its own merits.

4. Linux is a good OS and I use it a lot. But it has faults. If saying
that is FUD, so be it. Sue me.

PK

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Apr 17 13:28:47 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Apr 17 13:16:45 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] April Month ILUGC Meet

ILUGC Meet (Apr 21th):-
======================

Time : Sat Apr 21th 16:00 IST 2007
Venue: ADI-TeNeT Seminar Hall,
       #CSD 320, ESB, IIT-Madras.

Map: http://chennailug.org/tenet

Agenda:

> Talk 1:

Topic: Introduction to "Emacs Lisp - The Language"  By Sriram Karra

Abstract:

If there is one fundamental thing that distinguishes Emacs from its
competition, it is that the extension language for Emacs is a variant
of Lisp, a highly elegant and full blown high level functional
language. In this talk, we will explore the basic building blocks of
Emacs Lisp; at which level it is very similar to Common Lisp. We will
discover how it is different from other procedural languages, how many
of the 'modern' programming concepts in popular languages of the past
decade are really old ideas built into a fifty year young language.

This talk will not help you use Emacs better. However, you *cannot*
call yourself an expert Emacs user or realize its full potential
unless you can understand Lisp. This talk will certainly help you get
started on that life long journey. Further, the talk is *really* about
the language. So even if you never intend to use Emacs, come along if
you just want to know what all the hype about Lisp is.

Link: http://www.cs.utah.edu/~karra/tutorial

> Talk 2:

Topic: "Introduction to Haskell" By Rajagopal Natarajan

Abstract: 

This talk will cover the basics of Haskell and then on how well it
fits in for some real world applications like Music generation, Music
processing, Bio-informatics, etc.

Link: http://haskell.org/

Discussion about the dates for screening the MIT OCW Scheme video 
lectures.

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Tue Apr 17 18:22:14 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)

> From: Karanbir Singh <mail-lists@karan.org>

*WARNING* - LONG EMAIL

My point has always been:

1) Linux does NOT support BINARY-ONLY drivers. If you are contending that
pure BINARY drivers are supported on Linux, then I will need to see some
references/URLs for that. This has been discussed multiple times on the
kernel mailing lists and the Linux maintainers have consistently refused
to include support for BINARY-ONLY drivers in Linux. One of the reasons
stated against it is that it would violate GPL.

See:
http://www.kroah.com/log/linux/stable_api_nonsense.html

The Linux maintainers contend that *ALL* linux drivers must be part of the
Linux kernel source tree.

2) Binary drivers from companies such as Nvidia and ATI are supported via
kernel interface layers which are provided by these same companies. These
kernel interface layers are provided in two forms - a) Precompiled for
specific kernel versions b) In source form. If a precompiled version is
not available for your specific kernel release, then you must necessarily
compile the kernel interface layer and for this kernel version and for
this you will need a minimum of the kernel headers on your machine.

I am resending the links which will explain this:

See:
http://us.download.nvidia.com/XFree86/Linux-x86/1.0-9755/README/chapter-02-section-03.html

For ATI:
http://ati.amd.com/support/drivers/linux/linux-radeon.html
NOTE: Please notice the text on this page that mandates that kernel
headers are required if the entire kernel source is not present.

Also see:
http://linuxhelp.150m.com/ati/ati.htm

Address these points without using offensive language.

> Prem Kurian Philip wrote:
>> Please see:
>> http://www.microsoft.com/technet/prodtechnol/winxppro/maintain/sp2mempr.mspx
>
> that is sort of my point, the service packs are considered to be a major
> update, a sort of snapshot in time release.

So, whats your point?

The reason I had posted that link was to inform you that unlike what you
had stated, service packs do sometimes update the kernel as well.

And despite that, most *BINARY* drivers will still continue to work on
windows - you may come out and say that the driver for this one device or
two devices didn't work - but what you forget to mention is that the
drivers for literally 1000s of other devices continue to work without any
disruption even with a kernel update on windows. I am referring to
*BINARY-ONLY* drivers.

>>> "a lot of hardware out there is still not really running ok on Vista."

No, I am not referring to any packaging issue. I am referring to the fact
that the drivers have to be recompiled for each linux kernel release or
someone else has to provide the precompiled drivers for you for each
kernel release.

Also, see my initial set of points - Linux does NOT support BINARY-ONLY
drivers. This is NOT a packaging problem. Again, see my Point 1 at the top
of the email.

Let me repeat. It is NOT a packaging problem. Neither is it a delivery
problem and it has ABSOLUTELY NO bearing on whether Linux supports
binary-only drivers or not.


>>> It seems from your statements that you havent really ever used a stable
>>> distro before ? Could I ask what distro you really use ?
>>
>> I have used Linux since 1994 and I have used a variety of distros
>> starting
>> with slackware, Redhat, Suse, Mandrake, Vector, Fedora Core x etc.

> none of these are either considered enterprise grade or stable by anyone
> really. So my question still stands - have you used a stable enterprise
> distro ? eg. look at Suse - they had kabi stabalisation worked out
> before pretty much anyone - or look at centos-4 and the whitelisting /
> kabi assurance system built in. I fear you are making a lot of noise
> without actually having used a system that provides the very platform
> you are looking for.

I am not going to get into a pointless debate about what is a "stable"
distro. In anycase, that is not the point of the discussion.

Also, by the way, the architecture for the Linux kernel on poor "unstable"
distros such as slackware and those on the enterprise linuxes is the same.
What is different about the enterprise kernels is that some drivers may be
removed, some new drivers may be added in, some parameters may be tweaked
etc.

OK, I know there are additional tools:

for example:
http://developer.novell.com/wiki/index.php/Using_the_SLES9_kernel-update-tool_to_Update_Kernel_Modules

and differences in the userland etc in enterprise linuxes.. and also the
far more rigorous qualification process,  but I am constraining my
discussion to just the kernel for now.

Talking about kABI - that is just an acronym for Kernel Application Binary
Interface. When you refer to the "kabi assurance", I am guessing that you
are referring to the kABI notification system available for those such as
partners of the Novell Partner Linux Driver Process.

See:
http://developer.novell.com/wiki/index.php/Partner_Linux_Driver_Process

Under the Novell Partner Linux Driver Process, hardware vendors can
register their drivers with the Partner Linux Driver Process. When a user
tries to download a driver, YaST will check to see what version of the
driver to download (corresponding to the user's kernel version) and will
fetch the appropriate driver from the repository.

About kABI, kABI is NOT a mechanism which allows BINARY-ONLY drivers to
function across kernel updates on Linux.

About kABI, from Novell's site: "kABI Notification Service - The term
?kABI? refers to the kernel Application Binary Interface, the set of
in-kernel symbols used by drivers and other kernel modules. (kABI does not
refer to the syscall interface used by user-space programs). The
mainstream Linux kernel is a dynamic entity and as such, there are
frequent changes to the kABI. While SUSE Linux kernel engineering teams
endeavor to maintain a stable kABI between service pack releases, security
updates may occasionally necessitate kABI changes. As part of the PLDP,
the kABI notification service has been created to provide Novell partners
with information about how their modules could be affected by upcoming
kABI changes. The kABI Notification Service also allows the SUSE Linux
kernel engineering teams to proactively assess (as part of their research
process) how proposed kABI changes might affect partner modules.

When a partner submits kABI information for a module, Novell Partner
Engineering places the information in its partner module repository. For
each new kernel release, Novell/SUSE checks the module's symbols against
the new kernel's kABI, then sends the partner an email detailing any
observed kABI incompatibilities. The kABI Notification Service thus gives
partners the information they need to ensure that their drivers and kernel
modules will work with upcoming SUSE Linux kernel releases."

>>> I actually meant what I said, I have a single binary kernel module that
>>> drives my 3ware 9550, without needing a recompile, for 2 years and its
>> You seem to be unaware that all Linux kernel releases from 2.4.3 already
>> includes the 3ware 9550 driver.
>
> you seem to have pulled this one our of your ass really. I am running
> 2.6.9-EL branch on my home server, there was no 9550sx support in it
> till U4 really - and even then I continue to use the .ko since I have
> some xfs specific code in there.

If you are able to make a BINARY-ONLY driver work across kernel updates,
then that is a feature of Linux which even Linus Torvalds isn't aware off.

If there are *any* updates to the kernel headers, the driver depending on
them must be recompiled. There is no way around it.

> ( saw your email that 2.6.14 had the driver... thats ok, i dont use
> unstable upstream kernels :) )

> all, and hopefully they should adopt that soon.

users to use BINARY-ONLY drivers?

>> drivers which work across kernel releases. If the source driver for
>> 3ware
>> 9550 did not exist as part of the Linux kernel, you would have had to
>> download and install a binary version of the 3ware 9550 driver for each
>> version of linux kernel that you use.
>

> want to push that as an argument. And you seem to completely ignore the

There is a third option. c) You don't understand what I am saying (or may
be even a fourth) d) you choose not to.

>

>

I have posted information about this before. I post this again here.

For ATI:
http://ati.amd.com/support/drivers/linux/linux-radeon.html
NOTE: Please notice the text on this page that mandates that kernel

> My contention from the start has been that Linux does not support
> BINARY-ONLY drivers and that as the linux kernel is updated on a user's
> machine, he will need to recompile the drivers other than for one or two
> specific cases ( a. The kernel interface layer is provided by the vendor
> or b. The kernel headers and symbols remain exactly the same between the

completely ) I dont know why you continue to blow this horn... You are

really work on a stable distro :)

for their vmware-server download, is from the U1 days kernel on 
centos-4, they have not needed to rebuild anything since then, their 
drivers work fine for all kernels upto now. And to give you an idea of 
what that translates into, there have been over 900 modifications to the 
kernel since vmware built that .ko set ( bugfix, enhancements, new 
drivers being added, driver updates, stability fixs, security fixs etc ).

Subject: [Ilugc] Help regarding configuring NAT in Redhat Linux
Message-ID: <38b8d1a50704182239u424cc5a4l26ff7401d88aaa9b@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,
In my project I needed NAT for connecting to external LAN (not internet)
from internal LAN . For this, I created IP alias eth0:1 to the interface
eth0 of single NIC and trying to use that system as NAT.

The steps I followed are ;;

echo 1 > /proc/sys/net/ipv4/ip_forward

/sbin/iptables -t nat -A POSTROUTING -o eth0 -j MASQUERADE

/sbin/iptables -A FORWARD -i eth0 -o eth0:1 -m state --state
RELATED,ESTABLISHED -j ACCEPT

/sbin/iptables -A FORWARD -i eth0:1 -o eth0 -j ACCEPT


*In **/etc/sysctl.conf*  *net.ipv4.ip_forward = 1

while entering these commands, it is giving some kind of warning with eth0:1
about IP aliases

And later, the system in internal LAN is not pinging to the system in
external LAN. The NAT system itself is pinging well both to the internal and
external LANs.

Can you pls tell me wether I can use aliases for NAT and if yes how to
implement them using Iptables or some another way in Redhat Linux. Iam very
near to the project deadline and got stuck with this . Urgent pls help...

I am using RedHat Enterprise Linux -4.0 and just now I upgraded my system. When I enter a command su - username. It shows incorrect password. when I create a new user now also I could not switch to that user account. I searched all the solution for this issue in the net. It does not work. Kindly give me your suggestion.
   
   
  here is my /etc/pam.d/su file
   
  #%PAM-1.0
auth       sufficient   /lib/security/$ISA/pam_rootok.so
# Uncomment the following line to implicitly trust users in the "wheel" group.
#auth       sufficient   /lib/security/$ISA/pam_wheel.so trust use_uid
# Uncomment the following line to require a user to be in the "wheel" group.
#auth       required     /lib/security/$ISA/pam_wheel.so use_uid
auth       required     /lib/security/$ISA/pam_stack.so service=system-auth
account    required     /lib/security/$ISA/pam_stack.so service=system-auth
password   required     /lib/security/$ISA/pam_stack.so service=system-auth
# pam_selinux.so close must be first session rule
session    required     /lib/security/$ISA/pam_selinux.so close
session    required     /lib/security/$ISA/pam_stack.so service=system-auth
# pam_selinux.so open and pam_xauth must be last two session rules
session    required     /lib/security/$ISA/pam_selinux.so open multiple
session    optional     /lib/security/$ISA/pam_xauth.so
~

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Sun Apr 22 10:33:35 2007
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sun Apr 22 10:33:42 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] usb device driver
In-Reply-To: <d489eaf10704212023p1bcd8abcy78235520fb5f1324@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <295014.84809.qm@web50205.mail.re2.yahoo.com>

Hi,

--- Ashok Kumar <ashok.grpmail@gmail.com> wrote:
> Assume there is a kernel module for a simple usb
> device

What kernel module? What does it do? For what USB
device?

> (surely, this is not
> a block device).

USB is an interfacing protocol. Depending on the
device that is connected, the corresponding USB class
driver is used, which determines its mode of
operation. 

If you connect a USB thumb drive, then it is a mass
storage device, and /dev/sda1 (for example) is a block
device.

If you connect a USB-to-serial converter, you will use
/dev/ttyUSB0 (for example), which is a character
device.

> it does not have major and minor number assinged,

Then how will you access the device?

> instead it has attribute
> files on /sys directory. so that user application
> can access.

sysfs [1] provides device and driver information to
user-space, which is implemented as part of the driver
[2].

SK

[1] Sysfs. http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sysfs

[2] Chapter 14: The Linux Device Model. http://lwn.net/images/pdf/LDD3/ch14.pdf

--
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Mon Apr 23 14:21:32 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] usb device driver
In-Reply-To: <d489eaf10704230132y107e33f5i4ef6e21573521d75@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <940453.57106.qm@web50206.mail.re2.yahoo.com>

Hi Ashok,

--- Ashok Kumar <ashok.grpmail@gmail.com> wrote:
> you are not answered for my question on earlier
> post.

Your questions are too generic.

> it is possible to write a driver without major and
> minor numbers. right?

It depends on what context you mean by "driver" in the
above.

> we can access this driver through files on sysfs.
> right?

Again, what do you mean by "access"? There are no
files in /sysfs. It is a "virtual" filesystem. You can
only read/write variables exported by the driver (for
configuration) through sysfs. You didn't read Chapter
14: Linux Device Model [1]?

I'll stop here.

SK

[1] http://lwn.net/images/pdf/LDD3/ch14.pdf

From bhuvan at ubuntu.com  Tue Apr 24 10:36:07 2007
From: bhuvan at ubuntu.com (Bhuvaneswaran)
Date: Tue Apr 24 10:36:16 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Fwd: Community Council nominations and confirmation polls
In-Reply-To: <462C8659.2040204@ubuntu.com>
References: <462C8659.2040204@ubuntu.com>
Message-ID: <4dc6c9040704232206u5f65396fne1c6b10e4a47aea7@mail.gmail.com>

I know couple of Ubuntu Members are here. This is just an FYI. Please
cast your votes for electing one of new member for the Ubuntu
Community Council.

---------- Forwarded message ----------
From: Mark Shuttleworth <mark@ubuntu.com>
Date: Apr 23, 2007 3:41 PM
Subject: Community Council nominations and confirmation polls
To: ubuntu-news@lists.ubuntu.com
Cc: ubuntu-marketing@lists.ubuntu.com, ubuntu-doc@lists.ubuntu.com,
forums-council@lists.ubuntu.com,
ubuntu-devel-announce@lists.ubuntu.com, Ubuntu Art Team
<ubuntu-art@lists.ubuntu.com>



 Members of the Ubuntu community,

 We have 5 nominations to expand the community council, and voting starts today.

 Each candidate is standing individually, so there are 5 separate
votes. If a majority of the voters approve that candidate, then (s)he
will be confirmed as a new member of the CC with a two year term.

 I would urge all formal members of the Ubuntu community to vote. The
formal members are those who are currently listed at:

   https://launchpad.net/~ubuntumembers/

 The polls themselves are listed at:

   https://launchpad.net/~ubuntumembers/+polls

 Please vote in all polls where you have a personal opinion on the
candidate's contribution to Ubuntu and their competence to sit on our
top governing board. There are candidates from a variety of
significant communities within Ubuntu, such as the Forums and the
documentation team, but once confirmed to the CC they will represent
the community as a whole and not any particular subteam - even if they
retain a position in one of the other team councils of the project.

 The Community Council is our highest governing body of the project,
and makes fundamental decisions around our community structure, and
code of conduct. They serve to mediate disputes and also appoint the
leaders of key community teams.

 We specifically have 5 independent candidates because we believe that
it's important to have a broad coverage of timezones and areas of
expertise on the CC.

 I'd like to thank Dennis Kaarsemaker, the CC secretary, for setting
up the polls, and the candidates for their willingness to serve. I
would ask folks who lead various communities within Ubuntu to draw the
attention of their members to these polls so that we get the broadest
participation in each of the decisions.

 Mark

--
ubuntu-doc mailing list
ubuntu-doc@lists.ubuntu.com
https://lists.ubuntu.com/mailman/listinfo/ubuntu-doc

Balamurugan Murthy wrote:
> Hi All,
> 
> Is there any way to avoid file delete confirmation in unix ( apart
> from rm -rvf  option ) while using rm command ?
> 

Check the bashrc installed by your distro ($HOME/.bashrc or 
.bash_profile), most likely it has an alias for "rm".  Remove/Comment it.

From parth.technofreak at gmail.com  Tue Apr 24 14:31:36 2007

Date: Tue Apr 24 14:34:01 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] rm command
In-Reply-To: <b7640ce50704240145r1a2795emc4a5b1530fdb29e9@mail.gmail.com>
References: <b7640ce50704240145r1a2795emc4a5b1530fdb29e9@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <462DC770.6040800@gmail.com>

Balamurugan Murthy wrote:
> Hi All,
> 
> Is there any way to avoid file delete confirmation in unix ( apart
> from rm -rvf  option ) while using rm command ?

Confirmation of delete while using rm command is an added precaution 
from accidentally deleting something. I wonder why you want to bypass it ?

The easiest way it to create an alias named something like 'deleteyes' 
for the command "rm -rvf". Beware this can erase something without warning.

( I will personally suggest having a alias delete for 'rm -iv' and 
rather use it instead of rm)

From masatran at research.iiit.ac.in  Tue Apr 24 21:56:01 2007
From: masatran at research.iiit.ac.in (Masatran, R. Deepak)
Date: Tue Apr 24 21:56:25 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] rm command
In-Reply-To: <b7640ce50704240145r1a2795emc4a5b1530fdb29e9@mail.gmail.com>
References: <b7640ce50704240145r1a2795emc4a5b1530fdb29e9@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20070424162601.GA14694@research.iiit.ac.in>

* Balamurugan Murthy <balamurugan.murthy@gmail.com> 2007-04-24
> Is there any way to avoid file delete confirmation in unix ( apart
> from rm -rvf  option ) while using rm command ?

For safety (undo-ability), and neatness; un-alias "rm", and move
the-files-to-be-deleted to "/tmp" instead.

To also ensure privacy, create "~/tmp", move the-files-to-be-deleted to it
instead, and clean it up periodically.

Refer Powers; Peek; O?Reilly; Loukides, "Unix Power Tools"
<http://www.oreilly.com/catalog/upt3/> for relevant information.

-- 
Masatran, R. Deepak <http://research.iiit.ac.in/~masatran/>

This thread has become the 'horror stories' thread :)

If i need to use * or any expression for rm, i usually would type the command
with command name as 'm' or something, read it carefully, and then replace
m with rm, and press return - specially on a server. it sort of guards against
accidental return key press.

m: command not found.

well, i _try_ to follow that, not that i follow it every time.

I had my share of frustration as well. In one case my file was a text file,
and i had to use 'dd', read chunks, search through using grep .... it was very
painful,  but worth it because the document was very important. could
automate it to some extent, because i knew exact phrases from the doc.

>
> Hi,
>
> what is geographical addressing in PCI?


 Having the location of the device on board as part of the address. Like
having the slot no as part of the address, so that you can find out which
device is in a particular slot.

> and i had to use 'dd', read chunks, search through using grep .... it 
> was very
> painful,  but worth it because the document was very important. could
> automate it to some extent, because i knew exact phrases from the doc.
> 

I respect the original Unix philosophy that the user knows what he/she 
is doing.  So, thats why most of the commands are designed in such a way 
that they don't prompt whether you're sure about doing the "correct thing".

A lot of folks have had bad experiences (or probably never had the 
experience to work on the original SYSV or SunOS, Solaris with "lame" 
shells -- not even KSH) and have been much comfortable only with recent 
fancy shells like Bash/TCSH/...

Of course there are chances of typos, but I would just check the command 
I type before hitting the Return key.  I would never like something like 
"WARNING! Are you sure you want to delete all files? This action is not 
reversible!" when I'm invoking "rm *" -- of course I know what I'm doing 
damn it!!

Just my view of this "horror stories" thread.

-- 
Gopalarathnam Venkatesan

http://gopalarathnam.com/

From srivasta at debian.org  Wed Apr 25 18:54:01 2007
From: srivasta at debian.org (Manoj Srivastava)
Date: Wed Apr 25 18:54:56 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: rm command
References: <b7640ce50704240145r1a2795emc4a5b1530fdb29e9@mail.gmail.com>
	<200704250750.46499.kbalavignesh@gmail.com>
	<154eca020704242027if384989i1b332c907acdb654@mail.gmail.com>
	<462ED766.8090405@gopalarathnam.com> <462EF16F.6040901@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <87mz0wwpse.fsf@glaurung.internal.golden-gryphon.com>

Hi,

        I think zsh has the best of both worlds in this:
__> rm -rf *
zsh: sure you want to delete all the files in /tmp? (waiting ten seconds)
 [yn]? n
__> rm -rf foo*
__>

        So, it makes you wait for 10 seconds if you do rm -rf *, so no
 knee jerk responses are likely to make it through, but rm -rf of a
 smaller set (where you are likely to have considered what you are
 deleting) just go through.

        manoj

 RM_STAR_SILENT (-H) <K> <S>
        Do not query the user before executing ?rm *? or ?rm path/*?.

 RM_STAR_WAIT
        If querying the user before executing ?rm  *?  or  ?rm  path/*?,
        first  wait  ten seconds and ignore anything typed in that time.
        This avoids the problem of reflexively answering  ?yes?  to  the
        query  when  one  didn?t really mean it.  The wait and query can
        always be avoided by expanding the ?*? in ZLE (with tab).


-- 
Like I always say -- nothing can beat the BRATWURST here in DUSSELDORF!!

rajasekhar kuppa wrote:
> Hi,
> 
> as of this week entilre sun java stack is down loadable for Ubntu --
> starting with feisty-with just an apt-get
> 
> I  do under stand that  sun stack was not the way to go earlier-- but with
> this -- surely other linux implementations will follow?

Unlikely. Distributions which only want to include Free and open source 
software won't include the Sun stack unless it is free of proprietary 
encumbrances. Sun Java is not completely under a GPl+ Classpath 
exception license yet.

http://www.sun.com/software/opensource/java/faq.jsp#h

> i am not trying to  flame or some thing but i am really not good in this
> aspect -- so if there is some thing that iam missing . specially since you
> mention that  a make file for he identical binary that sun ships is not to
> be available - is ubuntu  being available with this  aolution to the
> predicament you mentioned  -- if not  how so ?

That particular distribution is merely including binaries with 
proprietary parts that a vendor provides without the complete source 
code under a Free and open source license. That isn't a solution for 
everyone.

Rahul

interest to adopt or encourage open source community. Obviously they
have commercial reasons for do this and it is one of the marketing
tactic to advertise their product.

For instance, Canonical is improving its launchpad community web site
tremendously. They do their own version control system, issue tracker,
polling system and many other components integrated in the web site.
If we closely watch the improvement, we get a feel that their
intention is to make it as a product for commercial reasons.

Subject: [Ilugc] Regarding Python File Function
In-Reply-To: <a54a308e0704270027p3d02e4b8q95b9a386954b90a1@mail.gmail.com>
References: <a54a308e0704270027p3d02e4b8q95b9a386954b90a1@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <9a9bfc170704270041p3badd5e0vb2bb44a7806bbc32@mail.gmail.com>

> How will one open a file with a mode "always create the file"

You cannot "always create the file" as the file could exist already...
Three solutions if the file already exists:

1. Truncate the file: Use "w"
2. Append to the file: Use "w+"
3. Return with the error: Not sure how to do this with fopen. But the
UNIX open with flags O_CREAT and O_EXCL will serve the purpose.

it moves on..

successful termination of their C programs.

to host open source projects. On the other hand, they may also
shutdown the service, if they have justifiable reasons, in which case,
the community may move to different hosting service provider. Anyway,

.

.

From anandsaha at gmail.com  Sat Apr 28 08:47:33 2007
From: anandsaha at gmail.com (Anand Saha)
Date: Sat Apr 28 08:47:41 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] scheduling in linux
In-Reply-To: <69621d830704271117o2ddc8d0ewd735c1441e65a832@mail.gmail.com>
References: <69621d830704271117o2ddc8d0ewd735c1441e65a832@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <154eca020704272017sc4b7242of53695168a080664@mail.gmail.com>

On 4/27/07, Zico <mailzico@gmail.com> wrote:
> I have to make a process scheduler in linux. The specification is something
> like this:
>
> The input will be taken from file. The input format is as follows:
>
> No of processes(N)
> arrival time cpuBurst IOBurst..........0.
> .
> .
> .
> (N such entries)
>
>
> The output will be in the following format:
> cpuUtilization
> Throughput
> Waiting time turnaround time
> .
> .
> .
> (N such entries)
>
> How can make it possible?

Let me get this correct. Have you been asked to write a scheduler for
linux (wow!) ? Or have you been asked to run some processes and do
accounting of the resources they used and their performance ?

If the later, you might use the /proc/<pid>/ to gather stats for the process.
man proc. You might as well use the various system calls to gather this
information. From what i can think of now, you might write a program
with fork() in it, so that the parent process can do the accounting, and
the child process can exec() the Nth intended process (out of your N
processes). The parent process can always monitor, because it knows
the pid of the child. (I am having strace in my mind - like it tells you
all the system calls your process makes).

If you want to set the scheduling policy for your process, you can use
sched_setscheduler(). man for it. The man page will show you other
useful function calls at the bottom.  Note: I have read about it, have
not used it.

Now after all this - i believe you might already have tools to do the
above :)) But its good to write your own program and understand stuff.

saha

Kenneth Gonsalves wrote:
> 
> On 27-Apr-07, at 5:21 PM, Rahul Sundaram wrote:
> 
>> Maybe a analogy would help. Microsoft Office is a product. Google 
>> Office (non enterprise edition) is a web service. That's the difference.
> 
> both are proprietary - so no real diff

Sure there is. The traditional norms of Free software have never 
involved web services and none of the licenses (except for Affero GPL) 
treat web services as a form of distribution.

There is a take at http://log.ometer.com/2006-07.html#29 on the impact. 
The latest GPL v3 draft at 
http://gplv3.fsf.org/gpl-draft-2007-03-28.html includes a compatibility 
provision with (yet to be released) Affero GPLv2. This along with the 
related rationale document explaining the changes shows that there is 
indeed a difference between a web service and a product.

Rahul

Qhwn you formatted the Suse partition, the boot loader was still GRUB.
Thus, it could not find the image to boot the OS and hence the error.
> then i installed kubuntu. got the boot loader correctly. but it
> shows my
> older suse linux which i removed and has removed the ubuntu6.10 from my

This is a bit confusing, when the Kubuntu installed where did the
Ubuntu 6.10 come from ? You said you have removed the Suse and the
GRUB should have got reinstalled now. So, it should point to the
current Kubutu installation. If not, you can manually edit GRUB's
menu.list to point to your Kubuntu installation.

Kubuntu = Ubuntu with KDE. You can have KDE (kubuntu-desktop) in
Ubuntu or Ubuntu (ubuntu-desktop) in Kubuntu installations. You want
KDE with Ubuntu or a seperate Kubuntu installation along with Ubuntu ?

boot the PC with the Ubuntu Live CD..

go to terminal..

$ sudo grub

it will take it the grub prompt,

> find /boot/grub/stage1

gives you locations..(if more than one)

chose the location where grub need to be installed..

then give,

> root (hd*,*)

then to install grub,

> setup (hd0)

Finall to quit,

> quit

Reboot the PC...:-)

>
is it not possible to have ubuntu and kubuntu together.
> what should i do to get my ubuntu back


It is possible.. I do have like that.. The grub boot loader (am not sure or
the debian installer)  which writes to the /boot/grub/menu.lst has some
problems in Ubuntu.

When one have a distro of Ubuntu already and tries to install another in
some other partition it creates more entries in this menu.lst

u can manually edit them and customize..

It is this menu.lst entriy that appears while we boot our PC... Check there
for your installations...

Hope this give some idea.. it helped me some time back :-)

From akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in  Sat Apr 28 17:00:04 2007
From: akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in (Kumar Appaiah)
Date: Sat Apr 28 16:51:28 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] RE: ubuntu desktop resolution problem
In-Reply-To: <20070428104742.BA9921DB259@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
References: <20070428104742.BA9921DB259@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <20070428113004.GA29529@localhost>

On Sat, Apr 28, 2007 at 04:17:32PM +0530, Muthukumar Prakasham wrote:
> I have accidentally setup my screen to to high a resolution on the ubuntu
> desktop, and it is showing out of range, how can I change it or interupt the
> boot process next time to change the screen resolution?

In the GRUB screen, press `e' to edit the kernel line, and add an `S'
to the end of the line, press enter and then `b' to boot. That should
take you to single user mode, and you can reconfigure xserver-xorg or
manually edit the /etc/X11/xorg.conf and go to the ordinary runlevel
using init 2.

HTH.

Kumar

Chennai - 600 036

Karanbir Singh wrote:
>
> all I am saying is that so far- its not there yet. it might be at some 
> point, but not now. ( overheard someone saying java-7 might be the 
> first real outing for a majority gpl'd sun java... dont quote me on 
> this, it was just a overheard detail at a social event )
>
> - KB
>
The Java 7 JVM and compiler are already developed under GPL as OpenJDK. 
These can be used to bootstrap the GNU Classpath Libraries. The Sun JDK 
Class libraries are not under GPL yet.

Sun said it would put Java class libraries under GPL except for code 
licensed from other companies by March. On reading Classpath developer 
blogs and Javalobby forums it seems the process will be completed in 
around a month. Even then there might be parts missing which would 
require reimplementation.

None of the ditros currently package the GPL portions of the Sun Java 
stack. They all seem to be waiting for the libraries to come under GPL. 
The Ubuntu packages in multiverse are repackaged JDK from the sun 
website and are distributed by Ubuntu under the old Java Distributor 
License.

Regards,
Senthil

Message-ID: <4633D14A.3030704@karan.org>

S. Senthil Anand wrote:
> The Java 7 JVM and compiler are already developed under GPL as OpenJDK. 
> These can be used to bootstrap the GNU Classpath Libraries. The Sun JDK 
> Class libraries are not under GPL yet.

interesting, so I am not the only person who's heard of this - gpl'd 
java end to end, within the life of java-7..

> None of the ditros currently package the GPL portions of the Sun Java 
> stack. They all seem to be waiting for the libraries to come under GPL. 

We've been in touch with Sun on this issue ( we = centos ). And there 
are a few legal grey areas as well, including the issue of assumed 
liability which is a major factor in business grade platforms. And no 
one really wants to take on that task.

> The Ubuntu packages in multiverse are repackaged JDK from the sun 
> website and are distributed by Ubuntu under the old Java Distributor 
> License.

We had a look at those as well - Sun was pushing it really hard, but 
again it was legal and not technical issues that prevented it from going 
out ( dev.centos.org actually did get some testing rpms as well )

- KB

Karanbir Singh : http://www.karan.org/ : 2522219@icq

On 4/29/07, Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com> wrote:

Are there no seeds for the torrent? Then downloading it from another
place is the only solution. Or if you think its a problem with
Ktorrent, try opening the torrent with another client and point the
"save to" location to where Ktorrent had saved it. Most bittorrent
clients can continue on a torrent saved by another client (I've tried
that with Azureus and uTorrent).

> Hi,
> Today i am installing Etch.
> I want to install Postfix and i gave the command
> apt-get install postfix.
>
> it says about unmet dependencies & they are
>  exim4-base: Depends: exim4-config (>= 4.30) but it is
> not going to be installed or exim4-config-2
> E: Broken packages
>  so i uncomment the line which is in
> /etc/apt/sources.list   deb http://security.debian.org
> stable/updates main contrib non-free
>
>
> then i gave apt-get update command , it gives errors
> like  W: Couldn't stat source package list
> http://security.debian.org stable/updates/main
> Packages
> (/var/lib/apt/lists/security.debian.org_dists_stable_updates_main_binary-i3
>86_Packages) - stat (2 No such file or directory)
>
> and
>
> E: Some index files failed to download, they have been
> ignored, or old ones used instead.
>
> what i have to do to install postfix and other
> packages?

I hope the Etch DVD you have everything within.
So comment all the external links in the source.list file.
Put only the entry for DVD.

Then give apt-get update.

Now install whatever you need from the DVD itself.
